The Proof That Substances Always Possess Accidents
Imam Nasafi proves substances always have accidents via spatial and motion categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the kalam theologians prove that material substances are never free from accidents by examining the necessary pairs of conjunction/separation and motion/rest.

Core Idea
Substances are never free from accidents because spatial relations and motion have no middle state.

Imam Nasafi builds on the established origination of accidents to examine material entities. He finds that substances are always accompanied by accidents such as conjunction, separation, motion, or rest. This lesson walks through his logical proof that it is impossible for a substance to lack these accidents.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the main claim
Read the Arabic passage once. Notice that the author first recalls that accidents are created, then examines substances to find them never devoid of accidents.
The claim is that substances are necessarily accompanied by accidents.
2
Understand the definitions of the four key terms
The passage defines conjunction, separation, motion, and rest. Pay attention to how conjunction and separation are opposites, and motion and rest are opposites.
Conjunction is contact with no space; separation is disjunction with space.
3
Grasp the logical argument using no-middle states
The author argues that for any two substances, there are only two possibilities regarding space: either there is space between them (separation) or not (conjunction). Similarly, for a body in a place, it is either moving or at rest. No third possibility exists.
This forces substances to always have one of these accidents.
4
Conclude the proof
Since substances always have either conjunction or separation, and either motion or rest, they cannot be free from accidents. This completes the proof that substances are always accompanied by accidents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إذا ثبت حدوث الأعراض وتقرر، فتأملنا بعد ذلك في حال الأعيان فوجدناها غير متعربة من الأعراض التي ثبت حدوثها بما لا شبهة فيه من الدلائل، ثم تأملنا فوجدنا تعريها عن الأعراض وخلوها عنها ممتنعا مستحيلا، وذلك لأنا رأينا الاجتماع والافتراق معنيين وراء المفترق والمجتمع، وكذا الحركة والسكون على ما بينا في فصل إثبات الأعراض ثم رأينا أن الاجتماع تماس الجوهرين حتى لا يكون بينهما مكان والافتراق تباين الجوهرين حتى يكون لثالث بينهما مكان، وقيل الاجتماع كون جوهر بجنب جوهر بحيث ليس بينهما حيز، والافتراق كون جوهر لا بجنب جوهر، والحركة هي الانتقال من مكان إلى مكان، والسكون هو القرار في مكان في زمانين فصاعدا ثم رأينا أن وجود جوهرين لا يخلو من أن يكون بينهما حيزا أو لا يكون، ومن أن يكون كل واحد منهما بجنب صاحبه أو يكون لا بجنب صاحبه، ولا يتصور بين هاتين الحالتين واسطة، فكان إذا خلو الجوهرين عن الاجتماع والافتراق محالا، وكذا عن الحركة والسكون لأن المتمكن في مكان، إما أن ينتقل عنه فيكون متحركا وإما أن يستقر فيه فيكون ساكنا، ولا واسطة بينهما، فإذا كان خلو الجواهر عنهما جميعا محال فإن قلت: أليس أن الجوهر عندكم في أول أحوال وجوده يكون خاليا عن الحركة والسكون جميعا، إذ هو عندكم في حال حدوثه ليس بمتحرك ولا ساكن، فما أنكرتم أنه في الأزل يكون خاليا عنهما؟ قيل عرف ببديهة العقل معرفة لا يعارضها شك أن الجوهر في حالة البقاء لا يخلو عن الحركة والسكون لأنه إما أن يكون في الزمان الثاني في المكان الذي كان فيه الزمان الأول، وإما أن يكون في غيره فإن كان في المكان الأول فهذا سكون، وإن كان في المكان الثاني فهو حركة، ولا يتصور خلوه عن ذلك فأما في أول أحوال وجوده فتلك حالة واحدة لم يتصل بها حالة أخرى ليكون فيها في المكان الأول فيكون ساكنا أو في مكان آخر فيكون متحركا وفي حالة البقاء الحكم بخلافه، يوضحه أن الحركة هي كونان في مكانين والسكون كونان في مكان واحد، وفي الحالة الأولى لن يتصور إلا كون واحد وهو ليس بحركة ولا بسكون، فأما في حالة البقاء فيوجد كونان، فلابد من أن يكون حركة أو سكونا، فإن سلمتم للجوهر حالة الحدوث فقد أقررتم بحدوث الجواهر، فوقعت لنا الغنية عن إثباته بالدليل، وإن لم تسلموا ذلك فلن يتصور عندكم خلو الجواهر عن الحركة والسكون، على أن عندنا في أول أحوال الوجود لن يخلو الجوهر عن الكون وهو عرض أن كان خلا عن الحركة والسكون، لما أن كل واحد منهما عرضان وهما كونان ويستحيل وجود كونين في حالة واحدة ووجود كون واحد كاف لاستحالة خلوه عن العرض
Then when the occurrence of accidents is established and determined, we considered thereafter the state of the [material] entities and found them not devoid of accidents which are established to be originated without doubt from the proofs. Then we considered and found their being stripped of accidents and their being free from them impossible and inconceivable. That is because we saw that conjunction and separation are two meanings beyond the conjoined and the separated, and likewise motion and rest as we clarified in the chapter on proving accidents. Then we saw that conjunction is the contact of two substances so that there is no space between them, and separation is the disjunction of the two substances so that there is a space for a third between them. It is said: conjunction is a substance being alongside a substance such that there is no intervening space between them, and separation is a substance not being alongside a substance. Motion is the transfer from place to place, and rest is the settling in a place for two or more times. Then we saw that the existence of two substances cannot avoid either having space between them or not, and either each one is alongside its companion or not alongside its companion, and no intermediate state between these two states is conceivable. Thus if the two substances are free from conjunction and separation it is impossible, and likewise motion and rest, because a thing located in a place is either to move from it (thus it is moving) or to settle in it (thus it is at rest), and no intermediate between them. So if the substances being free from both is impossible, then if you say: is it not that the substance according to you in the first state of its existence is free from motion and rest both, since it according to you at the moment of its occurrence is neither moving nor at rest? So why do you deny that it could be free from them in pre-eternity? It is said: It is known by the intuition of the intellect with a knowledge that no doubt opposes that the substance in the state of permanence is not free from motion and rest, because it either is in the second moment in the place where it was in the first moment, or it is in another place. If it is in the first place, that is rest; if it is in the second place, that is motion. And it is inconceivable for it to be free from that. As for the first state of its existence, that is a single state not connected to another state so that it could be in the first place (thus at rest) or in another place (thus moving). In the state of permanence the ruling is otherwise. It is clarified that motion is two states in two places, and rest is two states in one place. In the first state, only one state is conceivable, which is neither motion nor rest. In the state of permanence, two states exist, so it must be motion or rest. If you concede for the substance the state of origination, then you have acknowledged the origination of substances, and we are spared from proving it by argument. And if you do not concede that, then it is inconceivable for you that substances are free from motion and rest, because according to us in the first state of existence the substance is not free from the state, which is an accident, even if it is free from motion and rest, since each of the two [motion and rest] are two accidents and they are two states, and it is impossible for two states to exist in a single moment, and the existence of one state is sufficient to negate its being free from accident.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a proof that material substances (jawāhir) can never be free from accidents (a‘rāḍ). The argument proceeds as follows: First, the author recalls that the origination (ḥudūth) of accidents has already been established. Then he observes that material entities (‘a‘yān) are never found devoid of these originated accidents. In fact, it is impossible for them to be stripped of accidents. Why? Because every substance necessarily has either conjunction (ijtimā‘) or separation (iftirāq) with respect to another substance, and either motion (ḥaraka) or rest (sukūn) with respect to place. Conjunction and separation are defined as either contact or disjunction of two substances with no intervening space or with a space. Motion is transfer from place to place; rest is remaining in one place for at least two moments. For any two substances, there are only two possibilities regarding spatial relations: either there is space between them or not, and either each is alongside the other or not — no third possibility exists. Similarly, a body in a place is either moving (transitioning) or at rest (staying), with no intermediate. Therefore, substances cannot be free from these four accidents. An objection is raised: at the very first moment of existence, the substance is neither moving nor at rest; why could it not also be free from motion and rest in pre-eternity? The answer distinguishes between the first moment (state of origination) and subsequent moments (state of permanence, baqā’). In permanence, there are at least two moments, so the substance must either be in the same place (rest) or a different place (motion). In the first moment, there is only a single state (kawn), which is neither motion nor rest (since motion and rest require two states). The objector is forced into a dilemma: either they concede that the substance has a state of origination (thus admitting its createdness), or they deny that and must still accept that substances are never free from motion and rest — which also implies non-creation, but the author points out that even in the first moment the substance has a state (an accident), so it cannot be free from all accidents overall. Thus the proof that substances always have accidents stands, and this supports the doctrine that the world is created.

اجتماع (ijtima')
افتراق (iftiraq)
حركة (haraka)
سكون (sukun)
كون (kawn)

A) Transfer from place to place
B) Settling in a place for two or more times
C) A substance being alongside another substance
D) A substance not being alongside another substance

Key Takeaway
Substances always possess either conjunction or separation, and either motion or rest, so they can never be free from accidents.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Everything you see is composed of substances that are never free from accidents—constantly in conjunction, separation, motion, or rest. How does this truth expose the fragility and instability of the material world you rely on for security? Will you still anchor your heart in things that are perpetually changing, or will you seek the One who does not change?
?
Every breath you take involves movement and stillness, both created accidents from Allah. Does this awareness make you conscious that even your smallest actions are contingent upon His will? In what area of your life today can you consciously submit your motion and rest to His command?
?
The proof shows that two substances cannot exist without either being together or apart. Consider your relationships: they are also created realities, always in a state of either closeness or distance. Are you clinging to any relationship as if it were necessary and eternal, forgetting that all connections are contingent accidents? How can you redirect your attachment to the Eternal?

The First Moment Objection and Its Refutation
Imam Nasafi answers the objection about the first moment of a substance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that a substance at its first moment is free from motion and rest, and how the response distinguishes between the state of origination and the state of permanence.

Core Idea
The first moment has only one state; motion and rest require two moments.

An objector challenges the claim that substances always have motion or rest by pointing to the very first moment of a substance's existence, when it is neither moving nor at rest. Imam Nasafi answers by explaining that motion and rest are defined over two moments, whereas the first moment is a single state. This distinction preserves the rule for all subsequent moments and also forces the objector to admit the substance's creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
The objector says: according to you, the substance at the first moment is neither moving nor at rest, so why couldn't it be free from motion/rest in pre-eternity?
This objection tries to use the first moment as a counterexample.
2
Understand the answer: the distinction of permanence
The author responds that in the state of permanence (baqā'), which involves at least two moments, the substance must be either in the same place (rest) or a different place (motion).
The first moment is unique because it has no prior moment to compare.
3
Grasp the clarification using 'two states'
Motion is two 'states' (kawnān) in two places; rest is two states in one place. The first moment has only one state, so it cannot be motion or rest.
This technical point explains why the first moment is an exception.
4
See the dilemma presented to the objector
The author concludes: either you accept that the substance has a state of origination (thus it is created), or you must admit that even in the first moment it has an accident (the state itself), so substances are never accident-free.
Either way, the objector's position is undermined.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إذا ثبت حدوث الأعراض وتقرر، فتأملنا بعد ذلك في حال الأعيان فوجدناها غير متعربة من الأعراض التي ثبت حدوثها بما لا شبهة فيه من الدلائل، ثم تأملنا فوجدنا تعريها عن الأعراض وخلوها عنها ممتنعا مستحيلا، وذلك لأنا رأينا الاجتماع والافتراق معنيين وراء المفترق والمجتمع، وكذا الحركة والسكون على ما بينا في فصل إثبات الأعراض ثم رأينا أن الاجتماع تماس الجوهرين حتى لا يكون بينهما مكان والافتراق تباين الجوهرين حتى يكون لثالث بينهما مكان، وقيل الاجتماع كون جوهر بجنب جوهر بحيث ليس بينهما حيز، والافتراق كون جوهر لا بجنب جوهر، والحركة هي الانتقال من مكان إلى مكان، والسكون هو القرار في مكان في زمانين فصاعدا ثم رأينا أن وجود جوهرين لا يخلو من أن يكون بينهما حيزا أو لا يكون، ومن أن يكون كل واحد منهما بجنب صاحبه أو يكون لا بجنب صاحبه، ولا يتصور بين هاتين الحالتين واسطة، فكان إذا خلو الجوهرين عن الاجتماع والافتراق محالا، وكذا عن الحركة والسكون لأن المتمكن في مكان، إما أن ينتقل عنه فيكون متحركا وإما أن يستقر فيه فيكون ساكنا، ولا واسطة بينهما، فإذا كان خلو الجواهر عنهما جميعا محال فإن قلت: أليس أن الجوهر عندكم في أول أحوال وجوده يكون خاليا عن الحركة والسكون جميعا، إذ هو عندكم في حال حدوثه ليس بمتحرك ولا ساكن، فما أنكرتم أنه في الأزل يكون خاليا عنهما؟ قيل عرف ببديهة العقل معرفة لا يعارضها شك أن الجوهر في حالة البقاء لا يخلو عن الحركة والسكون لأنه إما أن يكون في الزمان الثاني في المكان الذي كان فيه الزمان الأول، وإما أن يكون في غيره فإن كان في المكان الأول فهذا سكون، وإن كان في المكان الثاني فهو حركة، ولا يتصور خلوه عن ذلك فأما في أول أحوال وجوده فتلك حالة واحدة لم يتصل بها حالة أخرى ليكون فيها في المكان الأول فيكون ساكنا أو في مكان آخر فيكون متحركا وفي حالة البقاء الحكم بخلافه، يوضحه أن الحركة هي كونان في مكانين والسكون كونان في مكان واحد، وفي الحالة الأولى لن يتصور إلا كون واحد وهو ليس بحركة ولا بسكون، فأما في حالة البقاء فيوجد كونان، فلابد من أن يكون حركة أو سكونا، فإن سلمتم للجوهر حالة الحدوث فقد أقررتم بحدوث الجواهر، فوقعت لنا الغنية عن إثباته بالدليل، وإن لم تسلموا ذلك فلن يتصور عندكم خلو الجواهر عن الحركة والسكون، على أن عندنا في أول أحوال الوجود لن يخلو الجوهر عن الكون وهو عرض أن كان خلا عن الحركة والسكون، لما أن كل واحد منهما عرضان وهما كونان ويستحيل وجود كونين في حالة واحدة ووجود كون واحد كاف لاستحالة خلوه عن العرض
Then when the occurrence of accidents is established and determined, we considered thereafter the state of the [material] entities and found them not devoid of accidents which are established to be originated without doubt from the proofs. Then we considered and found their being stripped of accidents and their being free from them impossible and inconceivable. That is because we saw that conjunction and separation are two meanings beyond the conjoined and the separated, and likewise motion and rest as we clarified in the chapter on proving accidents. Then we saw that conjunction is the contact of two substances so that there is no space between them, and separation is the disjunction of the two substances so that there is a space for a third between them. It is said: conjunction is a substance being alongside a substance such that there is no intervening space between them, and separation is a substance not being alongside a substance. Motion is the transfer from place to place, and rest is the settling in a place for two or more times. Then we saw that the existence of two substances cannot avoid either having space between them or not, and either each one is alongside its companion or not alongside its companion, and no intermediate state between these two states is conceivable. Thus if the two substances are free from conjunction and separation it is impossible, and likewise motion and rest, because a thing located in a place is either to move from it (thus it is moving) or to settle in it (thus it is at rest), and no intermediate between them. So if the substances being free from both is impossible, then if you say: is it not that the substance according to you in the first state of its existence is free from motion and rest both, since it according to you at the moment of its occurrence is neither moving nor at rest? So why do you deny that it could be free from them in pre-eternity? It is said: It is known by the intuition of the intellect with a knowledge that no doubt opposes that the substance in the state of permanence is not free from motion and rest, because it either is in the second moment in the place where it was in the first moment, or it is in another place. If it is in the first place, that is rest; if it is in the second place, that is motion. And it is inconceivable for it to be free from that. As for the first state of its existence, that is a single state not connected to another state so that it could be in the first place (thus at rest) or in another place (thus moving). In the state of permanence the ruling is otherwise. It is clarified that motion is two states in two places, and rest is two states in one place. In the first state, only one state is conceivable, which is neither motion nor rest. In the state of permanence, two states exist, so it must be motion or rest. If you concede for the substance the state of origination, then you have acknowledged the origination of substances, and we are spared from proving it by argument. And if you do not concede that, then it is inconceivable for you that substances are free from motion and rest, because according to us in the first state of existence the substance is not free from the state, which is an accident, even if it is free from motion and rest, since each of the two [motion and rest] are two accidents and they are two states, and it is impossible for two states to exist in a single moment, and the existence of one state is sufficient to negate its being free from accident.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a proof that material substances (jawāhir) can never be free from accidents (a‘rāḍ). The argument proceeds as follows: First, the author recalls that the origination (ḥudūth) of accidents has already been established. Then he observes that material entities (‘a‘yān) are never found devoid of these originated accidents. In fact, it is impossible for them to be stripped of accidents. Why? Because every substance necessarily has either conjunction (ijtimā‘) or separation (iftirāq) with respect to another substance, and either motion (ḥaraka) or rest (sukūn) with respect to place. Conjunction and separation are defined as either contact or disjunction of two substances with no intervening space or with a space. Motion is transfer from place to place; rest is remaining in one place for at least two moments. For any two substances, there are only two possibilities regarding spatial relations: either there is space between them or not, and either each is alongside the other or not — no third possibility exists. Similarly, a body in a place is either moving (transitioning) or at rest (staying), with no intermediate. Therefore, substances cannot be free from these four accidents. An objection is raised: at the very first moment of existence, the substance is neither moving nor at rest; why could it not also be free from motion and rest in pre-eternity? The answer distinguishes between the first moment (state of origination) and subsequent moments (state of permanence, baqā’). In permanence, there are at least two moments, so the substance must either be in the same place (rest) or a different place (motion). In the first moment, there is only a single state (kawn), which is neither motion nor rest (since motion and rest require two states). The objector is forced into a dilemma: either they concede that the substance has a state of origination (thus admitting its createdness), or they deny that and must still accept that substances are never free from motion and rest — which also implies non-creation, but the author points out that even in the first moment the substance has a state (an accident), so it cannot be free from all accidents overall. Thus the proof that substances always have accidents stands, and this supports the doctrine that the world is created.

Key Terms
حدوث (huduth)
بقاء (baqa')
كون (kawn)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The first moment of a substance's existence is a valid counterexample showing that substances can sometimes lack motion and rest.
Correction: The first moment is a special case with only one state; motion and rest require two states. In all subsequent moments (permanence), the substance must have one of them.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say that the first moment of a substance cannot be motion or rest?
A) Because motion and rest are both accidents that cannot exist at the same time.
B) Because motion is two states in two places and rest is two states in one place, but the first moment has only one state.
C) Because the substance is not yet fully created.
D) Because the first moment is in pre-eternity.

Key Takeaway
The first moment of a substance has only one state, which is neither motion nor rest, but in all subsequent moments it must have one of them, preserving the rule that substances always have accidents.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your existence began with a single state (kawn) that you did not choose. How does this humble you when you consider that your very being is a direct act of Allah's will, not your own? What would change in your daily attitude if you truly lived with this awareness?
?
The objector sought a loophole to avoid admitting that substances always have accidents. Are there areas in your faith where you look for loopholes to avoid submitting to the full implications of what you know to be true? What is one specific area where you need to stop seeking excuses and accept the truth?
?
The passage argues that every moment after the first involves a decision between motion and rest, each pointing to a continuous act of creation. How does your constant state of change—every heartbeat, every thought—remind you that you are always in need of Allah? What would it mean for you to respond to that need with reliance on Him right now?

First Argument: Substances Cannot Be Free from Accidents
Al-Nasafi argues against two ways substances could be free from accidents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Nasafi's first argument that substances cannot be free from accidents in pre-eternity, and why both possibilities lead to contradiction.

Core Idea
Freedom from accidents must be explained, but neither essence nor a meaning can justify it.

Al-Nasafi begins his proof for the existence of a creator by examining the nature of substances and accidents. He argues that substances cannot have been free from accidents in pre-eternity, because any explanation for such freedom leads to impossibility. This lesson unpacks his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation. Notice the logical structure and key terms.
Pay attention to the two possibilities: freedom by essence vs. freedom by a meaning.
2
Identify the two possibilities
Al-Nasafi presents two possible reasons for substances being free from accidents in pre-eternity. Locate them clearly.
The first is freedom by essence (li-dhātihā), the second is freedom by a meaning (li-maʿnā).
3
Follow the argument against freedom by essence
Understand why freedom by essence fails: if essence necessitates freedom, it cannot later accept accidents. The analogy with black and white helps.
4
Follow the argument against freedom by a meaning
See how the second possibility collapses: either the meaning remains (preventing accidents) or is removed (meaning is created, itself an accident).
This leads to the conclusion that substances cannot be free from accidents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يخلو عنه لا لذاته بل لقيام معنى مناف لذلك العرض في هذا المحل، كما يخلو الجسم عن السواد لقيام البياض به، وكذا على القلب وكذا عن الحركة والسكون وكل عرضين متضادين قام أحدهما في محل، فخلو الجواهر عن الأعراض في الأزل من أي قبيل كان أكانت الجواهر خالية عن الأعراض لذاتها أم كانت متعرية خالية عنها لمعنى؟ فإن كانت خالية لذاتها فما بالها قبلت الأعراض من بعد، والذات الموجب للتعري قائم؟ ولو جاز يقبل ذات عرضا مع قيام ما يوجب تعريه عنه، لجاز أن يقبل الجسم البياض مع قيام السواد به، إذ لا فرق بينهما في أن الموجب للتعري قائم إلا أن هناك الموجب هو الذات، وهاهنا الموجب هو معنى وراء الذات وهذا محال، فكذا الأول، وإن كانت الجواهر متعرية خالية عن الأعراض لمعنى ينافي الأعراض فلا يخلو الأمر إذا حدثت فيها الأعراض من ارتفاع ذلك المعنى أو إبقائه على ما كان، ومحال حدوث الأعراض فيها مع وجود المعنى الموجب لتعريه عنها، ولو جاز ذا لجاز اجتماع السواد والبياض وكل متضادين في محل، وإن ارتفع ذلك المعنى علم أنه كان محدثا لما أن العدم على القديم محال، وإذا كان محدثا كان عرضا والجوهر لا يخلو عنه أو عن الأعراض وهو في نفس عرض فإذا لم تخل الجواهر عن الأعراض ويستحيل خلوها عنها والله الموفق.
It is not free from it by its essence but due to the existence of a meaning that opposes that accident in this locus, just as the body is free from blackness due to the existence of whiteness in it, and similarly for opposites, and likewise for motion and rest, and every two opposing accidents when one of them exists in a locus. So the freedom of substances from accidents in pre-eternity is of which kind: were the substances free from accidents by their essences or were they bare and free from them due to a meaning? If they were free by their essences, then why did they accept accidents afterwards while the essence that necessitates freedom is present? And if it is permissible for an essence to accept an accident while that which necessitates its freedom is present, then it would be permissible for a body to accept whiteness while blackness is present with it, for there is no distinction between them in that the necessitator of freedom is present, except that there the necessitator is the essence, and here the necessitator is a meaning beyond the essence; and this is impossible. So likewise the first [case]. And if the substances were bare and free from accidents due to a meaning that opposes accidents, then when accidents occur in them, the matter cannot but be either the removal of that meaning or its preservation as it was. The occurrence of accidents in them while the meaning that necessitates their freedom exists is impossible; and if that were permissible, then the conjunction of blackness and whiteness and every pair of opposites in a locus would be permissible. And if that meaning is removed, it is known that it was originated, for non-existence of the eternal is impossible; and if it was originated, it was an accident, and a substance is not free from it or from [other] accidents, and it is itself an accident. So if substances are not free from accidents and their being free is impossible, and God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage presents the first of two arguments for the impossibility of substances (jawāhir) being free from accidents (aʿrāḍ) in pre-eternity (al-azal). The author begins by noting that a thing may be free from an accident not by its own essence but due to a meaning (maʿnā) that opposes that accident in that locus, using the example of a body being free from blackness because whiteness is present. He then poses a crucial question: in pre-eternity, when substances were allegedly free from all accidents, was this freedom due to the substances' own essences, or due to a meaning that opposes accidents?

First possibility: if substances are free by essence, then why did they later receive accidents? The essence that necessitated freedom is still present, so receiving accidents would be contradictory. He argues that if an essence can receive an accident despite the presence of what necessitates its freedom, then it would be permissible for a body to be simultaneously black and white—which is absurd. Since the only difference between the two cases is that in the first the necessitator is the essence and in the second a meaning, the impossibility in the second (simultaneous opposites) applies to the first as well.

Second possibility: if substances are free due to a meaning that opposes accidents, then when accidents arise, that meaning must either remain or be removed. If it remains, accidents cannot occur, as the meaning opposes them; this would imply that opposites coexist, which is impossible. If it is removed, then that meaning must have been originated (muḥdath), since it went from existence to non-existence—and non-existence of the eternal is impossible. As an originated thing, it is an accident, and a substance cannot be free from it or from other accidents. Thus, in both cases, substances cannot be free from accidents in pre-eternity.

Key Terms
الجواهر
الأعراض
الأزل
التعري
الذات
المعنى
التضاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the argument assumes the existence of accidents in pre-eternity.
Correction: The argument only examines the logical implications of the two possible ways a substance could be free from accidents; it does not assume accidents exist in pre-eternity.

Checkpoint
According to the first argument, if substances were free from accidents in pre-eternity due to their own essences, what would be the problem when they later receive accidents?
A) The essence would have changed.
B) The essence that necessitates freedom is still present, so receiving accidents would be contradictory.
C) The accidents would be eternal.
D) The substances would no longer be substances.

Key Takeaway
Substances cannot be free from accidents in pre-eternity, because any explanation for such freedom leads to logical impossibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If pre-eternal freedom from accidents is impossible, then your very existence as a being with accidents (your body, thoughts, feelings) is a sign that you are not self-sufficient. What are you relying on to maintain your existence today? Have you genuinely acknowledged that every moment you are sustained by the Creator, or do you live as if you are independent?
?
The argument shows that any freedom from accidents requires a cause outside the essence. In your spiritual life, where have you assumed you are 'free' from sin, doubt, or heedlessness by your own nature, rather than by a cause outside you—i.e., God's grace? How can you more consciously attribute your freedom from evil to Him?
?
This reasoning leads to the conclusion that the world is created and dependent. If you truly believe this, then your attachment to worldly things must be secondary to your attachment to the Creator. What worldly thing— a relationship, a possession, a status— are you acting as if it is independent and necessary, rather than a temporary accident sustained by God? Will you reorient your heart today?

The Second Argument: Successive Accidents Without Intermediate
Al-Nasafi presents a self-evident argument for the impossibility of substances being free from accidents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Nasafi's second argument for the necessity of accidents in substances, based on the self-evident impossibility of removing successive accidents without an intermediate.

Core Idea
If two opposites can't coexist, then two successive accidents can't both be removed.

This argument appeals to innate reason, using everyday examples like motion and rest or conjunction and separation. Al-Nasafi emphasizes that this principle is known to all rational minds, not just theologians. By comparing it to the impossibility of opposites coexisting, he reinforces that substances cannot be free from accidents.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once, noticing the key terms and the flow of the argument. Then read the translation to ensure understanding.
The passage is dense but uses common examples.
2
Identify the key examples
Notice the two pairs: conjunction/separation for two substances, and motion/rest for a body in a place. These are successive accidents without an intermediate.
These examples illustrate the principle clearly.
3
Understand the analogy to opposites
Al-Nasafi compares the impossibility of removing these successive accidents to the impossibility of two opposites coexisting in one locus. This analogy shows the strength of the argument.
The comparison is 'like' (ka) — it's a direct analogy.
4
Grasp the logical implication
If removing successive accidents were possible, then opposites could coexist. Since the latter is absurd, the former is also impossible. This proves that substances always have accidents.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأن استحالة ارتفاع العرضين المتعاقبين اللذين لا واسطة بينهما كالاجتماع والافتراق عن الجوهرين والحركة والسكون مع وجود المكان المتمكن عن المحل متقررة في بداية العقل وشهادات المعارف لا تفرقة فيه بين الرايض والمرتاض والعقل الخالي عن صناعة الكلام والحاذق الماهر فيه كاستحالة اجتماع المتضادين في محل واحد فلو جاز ذا لجاز هذا، وإذا استحال هذا وامتنع وخرج القول به عن قضية العقول استحال ذلك أيضا وامتنع والله الموفق.
And because the impossibility of the removal of two successive accidents between which there is no intermediate, such as conjunction and separation from two substances, and motion and rest with the existence of [؟] place from the locus, is established at the beginning of reason and the testimonies of cognitions—there is no distinction in it between the trained and the untrained, and the mind free from the craft of kalām and the skilled master thereof—like the impossibility of the conjunction of opposites in a single locus. So if this were permissible, that would be permissible; and if this is impossible and prohibited and its assertion falls outside the judgment of intellects, then that is also impossible and prohibited, and God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage presents a second, more intuitive argument for the impossibility of substances being free from accidents. The author appeals to self-evident reason: it is impossible for two successive accidents that have no intermediate between them—like conjunction and separation in two substances, or motion and rest in a body when space is present—to be simultaneously removed. This is known at the very beginning of rational thought and by the testimony of common cognitions, with no difference between the untrained person and the skilled theologian. He likens this impossibility to the impossibility of two opposites coexisting in one locus. The argument is by analogy: if the removal of such successive accidents were possible, then the coexistence of opposites would also be possible—but the latter is absurd, so the former is also absurd. Thus, the impossibility of substances being free from accidents is reinforced by this self-evident principle.

Key Terms
استحالة
ارتفاع
العرضين المتعاقبين
الواسطة
الاجتماع والافتراق
الحركة والسكون
بداية العقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument relies on specialized kalām terminology and is only convincing to trained theologians.
Correction: Al-Nasafi explicitly states that this principle is known at the beginning of reason and to all rational minds, trained or untrained.

Checkpoint
What does al-Nasafi compare the impossibility of the removal of two successive accidents without an intermediate to?
A) The impossibility of a substance existing without accidents.
B) The impossibility of the conjunction of opposites in one locus.
C) The impossibility of motion and rest coexisting.
D) The impossibility of an accident being eternal.

Key Takeaway
Al-Nasafi's second argument shows that the impossibility of removing successive accidents without an intermediate is as self-evident as the impossibility of opposites coexisting, proving that substances always have accidents.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are at every moment either in motion or rest, either breathing in or out. There is no instant you are without some quality. How does this constant, inescapable change remind you that you are not self-sufficient? Will you let this self-evident truth lead you to acknowledge your dependence on Allah in every second of your life?
?
The argument says that the impossibility of being free from accidents is as clear as the impossibility of opposites coexisting. Yet many people live as if they are independent, as if their existence is not a chain of dependent moments. Is there an area of your life where you rationalize away this obvious dependence? What would it cost you to fully submit to Allah's constant sustenance today?
?
If a substance cannot exist without an accident, then your very body is a proof of your contingency. When you look at your hand, it is either moving or still. How does this immediacy of proof challenge your pride? Will you, right now, say a prayer of gratitude to the One who holds you in existence from one moment to the next?

Pre-Eternity and the Timelessness of Impossibility
Al-Nasafi refutes an objection about pre-eternity using the principle that impossibility is timeless.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the impossibility of substances being free from accidents applies equally to pre-eternity and the present, and how the author uses the timelessness of impossibility to refute the objection.

Core Idea
Impossibility does not change with time — if it is impossible now, it was impossible in pre-eternity.

This lesson presents a key objection-and-answer from al-Nasafi's Tabṣirat al-Adilla. The objector grants that substances cannot be free from accidents in the present, but wonders whether pre-eternity might be different. Al-Nasafi's reply grounds the discussion in a timeless principle: what is impossible is impossible for all times. He illustrates this with the striking example of the conjunction of opposites.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the objection carefully: the objector concedes present impossibility but questions whether pre-eternity is under the same rule.
2
Grasp the author's principle
Notice the key statement: 'what is impossible does not change by state or condition.' This is the core of the response.
3
Examine the analogy of opposites
Consider the example of the conjunction of opposites (e.g., a body being both moving and still). Why would it be absurd to say such a thing was possible in pre-eternity?
4
See how the analogy resolves the objection
The same logic applies to substances and accidents: if free-from-accidents is impossible now, it cannot have been possible in pre-eternity.
5
Reflect on the role of rational judgment
The author appeals to 'qadiyyat al-ʿuqūl' (the judgment of intellects) as the final arbiter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل إن استحال خلو الجواهر عن الأعراض الآن فلم قلتم : إنه يستحيل في الأزل؟ قلنا : لأن ما يستحيل لا يتبدل بحال وحال أليس أن من قال: إن الجمع بين المتضادين يستحيل للحال وكان غير مستحيل في الأزل، وكانت الأجسام في الأزل مجتمعة متفرقة متحركة ساكنة سوداء بيضاء كان قوله مردودا فاسد في قضية العقول فكذا هذا والله الموافق.
For it might be said: If the impossibility of substances being free from accidents is [established] now, why do you say that it is impossible in pre-eternity? We say: Because what is impossible does not change by state or condition. Is it not that whoever says that the conjunction of opposites is impossible now but was not impossible in pre-eternity, and [says] that bodies in pre-eternity were both combined and separated, moving and still, black and white—his statement would be rejected and corrupt in the judgment of intellects? So likewise this. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer pair. The objector concedes that substances might be impossible to be free from accidents in the present, but questions whether this impossibility also applies to pre-eternity (al-azal). The author responds by asserting a foundational principle: what is impossible (mustaḥīl) does not change depending on time or state. To illustrate, he draws an analogy: if someone claimed that the conjunction of opposites (al-jamʿ bayn al-muḍādayn) is impossible now but was possible in pre-eternity, and that bodies in pre-eternity were simultaneously combined and separated, moving and still, black and white—that claim would be rejected outright by rational judgment. Similarly, the impossibility of substances being free from accidents cannot be restricted to the present; it holds for all times, including pre-eternity. The objection fails because logical necessity is timeless.

D) He says that substances in pre-eternity were different from substances now.

Key Takeaway
Impossibility is timeless: what is impossible now was always impossible, even in pre-eternity.

?

?
The objector tried to limit Allah's judgment to the present moment. In what area of your life do you act as if Allah's standards change with the times? What concrete step will you take today to submit to His timeless rule?

Proof That Substances Are Originated from Their Inseparability from Accidents
Al-Nasafi proves that substances must be originated because they cannot precede originated accidents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi proves that substances are originated by establishing that they cannot be prior to originated accidents.

Core Idea
Substances are originated because they cannot precede what is originated.

Al-Nasafi builds on the earlier conclusion that substances are never free from accidents. From this, he argues that substances cannot be prior to accidents, and since accidents are already proven originated, substances must share that originated status. This lesson unpacks the logical chain of that proof.

Guided Path
1
Review the premise: substances cannot be free from accidents
Recall that the impossibility of substances being devoid of accidents was established earlier. This is the foundation.
2
Show that substances cannot be prior to accidents
If substances cannot be free from accidents, they cannot exist before accidents, because priority would require a time when they were free of accidents.
3
Recall that accidents are originated
The author takes as given that accidents are originated (ḥāditha), proven elsewhere in the text. This is a key premise.
4
Apply the principle: whatever does not precede an originated thing is itself originated
Since substances do not precede originated accidents, they must be originated. The author defends this by defining 'originated' as having a beginning of existence.
This is the core logical step. If something had no beginning, it would precede everything that has a beginning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا ثبت استحالة خلو الجواهر عن الأعراض، ثبت استحالة تقدمها على الأعراض لما أن في تقدمها على الأعراض خلوها عنها ، وقد بينا استحالته، وإذا ثبت أن الجواهر لا تسبق الأعراض وأقمنا الدلالة على كون الأعراض حادثة فإذا لم يسبقها الجواهر كانت حادثة لأن ما لم يسبق الحادث حادث، لأن الحادث ما لوجوده ابتداء أو ما لم يكن ثم كان وما لم يسبق ما لوجوده ابتداء كان لوجوده أيضا ابتداء، إذ لو لم يكن لوجوده ابتداء لسبق ما لوجوده ابتداء وإذا كان لوجوده ابتداء كان محدثا ، وهذا لأن العرض كان محدثا لهذا فما ساواه
And when the impossibility of substances being free from accidents is established, the impossibility of their being prior to accidents is established, because in their being prior to accidents there is their being free from them, and we have shown its impossibility. And when it is established that substances do not precede accidents, and we have established the proof that accidents are originated, then if substances do not precede them, they are originated, because that which does not precede an originated thing is originated. For the originated is that whose existence has a beginning, or that which was not and then was; and that which does not precede that whose existence has a beginning itself has a beginning of existence, because if it did not have a beginning of existence, it would precede that which has a beginning of existence. And if it has a beginning of existence, it is originated. And this is because the accident was originated in relation to this [substance], so that which equals it [in temporality] ...
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage constructs the final proof that substances (jawāhir) are originated (ḥāditha). The author builds on the previous conclusion that substances cannot be free from accidents (aʿrāḍ). From this, it follows that substances cannot be temporally prior to accidents, because priority would require them to exist without accidents at some point, which has been shown impossible. Next, the author takes as given that accidents are originated (ḥāditha)—a point established elsewhere (perhaps earlier in the text). If substances do not precede accidents, and accidents are originated, then substances must themselves be originated. The reasoning is: whatever does not precede an originated thing is itself originated. The author clarifies the definition of 'originated' (al-ḥādith): it is that whose existence has a beginning (ibtidāʾ), or that which was not and then came to be. If a thing does not precede something that has a beginning of existence, then it too must have a beginning of existence—otherwise it would be prior to that which has a beginning, which is contradictory. Therefore, substances have a beginning of existence, i.e., they are originated. The final sentence suggests that since the accident is originated relative to the substance, the substance shares the same temporal status.

Key Terms
استحالة خلو الجواهر عن الأعراض
تقدم الجواهر على الأعراض
حادث
الابتداء
المحدَث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument only shows that substances coexist with accidents in time, not that they are originated.
Correction: The argument defines 'originated' as anything that does not precede an originated thing. Since substances do not precede originated accidents, they meet the definition of originated, regardless of whether they coexist.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why must substances be originated?
A) Because they are composed of atoms.
B) Because they cannot precede accidents, and accidents are originated.
C) Because they are material.
D) Because they change over time.

Key Takeaway
Substances are proven originated because they cannot be prior to originated accidents.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If everything around you—including your own body and mind—is originated and has a beginning, what does that mean for your feeling of self-sufficiency? Are you living as if you created yourself, or as a creature utterly dependent on the Creator?
?
The proof shows that you cannot be prior to the originated events of your life (your birth, your first moment). How does that truth challenge any pride or sense of eternal self-importance you might hold?
?
Since you are an originated being, your existence is not necessary—it could have been otherwise. How would your daily choices change if you truly internalized that every moment you exist is a gift from the One who brought you into being?

Impossibility is Absolute, Not Relative to Time
Nasafi refutes the objection that impossibility of substances being devoid of accidents is limited to the present.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi argues that the impossibility of substances being devoid of accidents is not limited to the present but applies to all states, including pre-eternity.

Core Idea
Impossibility does not change with time or state.

In this passage, Nasafi addresses an objection: perhaps substances could have been devoid of accidents in pre-eternity even though it's impossible now. He refutes this by establishing that true impossibility is absolute and unchanging. The example of combining opposites illustrates the absurdity of claiming impossibility is time-dependent.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
The objector asks why impossibility now must extend to pre-eternity. This sets up the challenge Nasafi must answer.
2
Understand Nasafi's principle
Nasafi states that what is impossible does not change from state to state. This is the core argument.
Impossibility is a fixed attribute of a proposition.
3
Examine the example of opposites
Nasafi uses the example of combining opposites to show the absurdity of claiming impossibility can change with time.
If one claimed opposites could coexist in pre-eternity, that would be rejected by reason.
4
Apply the analogy
The same logic applies to substances and accidents: if it is impossible now, it was always impossible.
This concludes the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل إن استحال خلو الجواهر عن الأعراض الآن فلم قلتم : إنه يستحيل في الأزل؟ قلنا : لأن ما يستحيل لا يتبدل بحال وحال أليس أن من قال: إن الجمع بين المتضادين يستحيل للحال وكان غير مستحيل في الأزل، وكانت الأجسام في الأزل مجتمعة متفرقة متحركة ساكنة سوداء بيضاء كان قوله مردودا. فاسد في قضية العقول فكذا هذا (۲). والله الموافق.
If it is said: The impossibility of substances being devoid of accidents now, so why do you say it is impossible in pre-eternity? We say: Because what is impossible does not change from state to state. Is it not that whoever says that the combination of opposites is impossible in the present while it was not impossible in pre-eternity, and that bodies in pre-eternity were combined, separate, moving, stationary, black, white, his statement is rejected, corrupt in the judgment of intellects. So likewise this. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer. The objector argues that the impossibility of substances being devoid of accidents might only apply to the present state, but not necessarily to the pre-eternal state (al-azal). The answer establishes a principle: impossibility is not subject to change based on time or state. If something is impossible now, it is impossible in all states. Nasafi supports this with an example: if someone claimed that combining opposites is impossible now but was possible in pre-eternity, that would lead to absurdities like bodies being simultaneously combined and separate, moving and stationary, black and white in pre-eternity. Such a claim is rejected by reason. Hence the same applies to substances being devoid of accidents.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Impossibility can change with time; something impossible now might have been possible in pre-eternity.
Correction: Nasafi argues that true impossibility is absolute and does not vary with time or state, as shown by the absurdity of claiming opposites could coexist in pre-eternity.

Checkpoint
What principle does Nasafi use to refute the objection that the impossibility of substances being devoid of accidents is only for the present?
A) Impossibility changes with time.
B) Impossibility is not subject to change based on state.
C) Substances can be devoid of accidents in pre-eternity.
D) Accidents are eternal.

Key Takeaway
Impossibility is a fixed attribute of a proposition and does not vary with time or state.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

This lesson teaches that impossibility does not change with state. How does that challenge your view of your obligations? What specific command have you been postponing that you now realize must be treated as absolutely required?
?
The objector thought impossibility could change. In your own life, where have you acted as if something was impossible now but possible later—like giving up a habit or fulfilling a duty? What step can you take today to treat that impossibility as absolute and seek Allah's help to overcome it?

The Creation of Substances from Their Inseparability from Accidents
Nasafi proves the creation of substances from their inseparability from created accidents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's argument that substances are created because they cannot precede created accidents, and his refutation of the Dahriyya objection.

Core Idea
What does not precede the created is itself created.

In this passage, Nasafi builds on the previously established impossibility of substances existing without accidents. He uses this to prove that substances are created, and he answers a materialist objection. Let's trace the logic step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text slowly. Then read the literal translation to grasp the argument.
Notice the logical connectors like 'idha thabata' and 'li-anna'.
2
Identify the main premise
Find the statement that substances cannot be devoid of accidents. Then see how it leads to the conclusion that substances are created.
The key step is that if substances precede accidents, they would be devoid of them, which is impossible.
3
Understand the objection and response
Read the Dahriyya objection and Nasafi's refutation. Note the distinction between the cause of being an accident and the cause of being created.
The example of Zayd and 'Amr illustrates the point.
4
Apply the principle
Reflect on the principle 'what does not precede the created is created'. Consider how this applies to substances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤ - إذا ثبت استحالة خلو الجوهر عن الأعراض: ارتباط الجوهر بالعرض] وإذا ثبت (۳) استحالة خلو الجواهر عن الأعراض، ثبت استحالة تقدمها على الأعراض لما أن في تقدمها على الأعراض خلوها عنها ، وقد بينا استحالته، وإذا ثبت أن الجواهر لا تسبق الأعراض وأقمنا الدلالة على كون الأعراض حادثة فإذا (٤) لم يسبقها الجواهر كانت حادثة لأن ما لم يسبق الحادث حادث، لأن الحادث (٥) ما لوجوده ابتداء أو ما لم يكن ثم كان وما لم يسبق ما لوجوده ابتداء كان لوجوده (٦) أيضا ابتداء، إذ لو لم يكن لوجوده ابتداء لسبق ما لوجوده ابتداء (۷) وإذا كان لوجوده ابتداء كان محدثا ، وهذا لأن العرض كان محدثا لهذا فما ساواه (۸) في حد الحدوث كان مساويا إياه في الحدوث، وبهذا يبطل اعتراض الدهرية أن الجوهر لما لم يكن عرضا لأنه لم يسبق العرض لم يشاركه فيما كان لأجله عرضا فإنه بعد سبقه إياه لم يصر مستحيل البقاء ولا مفتقرا في وجوده إلى محل، فلما لم يشاركه فيما له كان العرض عرضا لم (۱) يشاركه فى كونه عرضا، وهاهنا(۲) شاركه لعدم سبقه إياه فيما لأجله كان العرض ،حادثا، شاركه(۳) في كونه حادثا، وهذا لأن التساوي في الأحكام يكون عند (٤) التساوي في العلل لا عند التساوي في غير العلل، والجواهر لعدم السبق شاركت الأعراض في علة كونها حادثة، فكانت حادثة مثلها ، ولم تشاركها في علة كونها عرضا فلم تكن عرضا، والله الموفق. مثاله: أنا لو علمنا أن ولادة زيد كانت مقترنة بولادة عمرو ثم ثبت أن زيدا ابن (۹) عشرين سنة أوجب ذلك أن يكون عمرا، ابن عشرين سنة، ولم يوجب أن يكون زيد هو عمرو ولا أن ولادة زيد ولادة عمرو،
4. If the impossibility of the substance being devoid of accidents is established: The connection of substance to accident. And if the impossibility of substances being devoid of accidents is established, the impossibility of their preceding accidents is established, because in their preceding accidents there is their being devoid of them, and we have shown its impossibility. And if it is established that substances do not precede accidents, and we have given the proof that accidents are created, then since substances do not precede them, they are created, because what does not precede the created is created. Because the created is that whose existence has a beginning, or that which was not then was. And what does not precede that whose existence has a beginning also has a beginning for its existence, because if it did not have a beginning for its existence, it would precede that which has a beginning. And if it has a beginning for its existence, it is originated (muhdath). And this is because the accident was originated for this, so what equals it in the limit of origination equals it in origination. And by this the objection of the Dahriyya is invalidated, that since the substance was not an accident because it did not precede the accident, it did not share in that for which the accident is an accident, for after it preceded it, it did not become impossible of remaining nor dependent in its existence on a place. So since it did not share in that for which the accident is an accident, it does not share in being an accident. And here it shares due to its lack of precedence in that for which the accident was created, so it shares in being created. And this is because equality in judgments occurs when there is equality in causes, not when there is equality in non-causes. And substances, due to lack of precedence, share with accidents in the cause of being created, so they are created like them, and they do not share with them in the cause of being accidents, so they are not accidents. And God is the Grantor of success. Example: If we knew that the birth of Zayd coincided with the birth of 'Amr, then it is established that Zayd is twenty years old, that requires that 'Amr be twenty years old, and it does not require that Zayd is 'Amr or that Zayd's birth is 'Amr's birth.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage is a proof that substances (jawahir) are created (haditha). The argument proceeds as follows: It has already been proved that substances cannot be devoid of accidents (a'rad) at any time. From this it follows that substances cannot temporally precede accidents, because preceding would require a state of being devoid of accidents, which is impossible. Since accidents are proven to be created, and substances do not precede them, substances must also be created. The reasoning is that anything that does not precede the created is itself created; otherwise it would be eternal and would precede the created. Nasafi then refutes an objection from the Dahriyya (materialists) who argue that since substances are not accidents, they do not share the characteristics that make accidents accidents (such as being impermanent and dependent on a subject). Nasafi responds by distinguishing between the cause of being an accident and the cause of being created. Substances share with accidents in the cause of being created (namely, not preceding other created things), but they do not share in the cause of being accidents. Thus they are created without being accidents. He illustrates with an analogy: if two births coincide and one person is known to be twenty years old, the other must also be twenty, but they are not the same person. Similarly, substances and accidents are both created, but substances are not accidents.

Key Terms
جوهر
عرض
حدوث
تقدم
دهرية
علة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Substances are not accidents, so they are not created like accidents.
Correction: Nasafi argues that the cause of creation (not preceding created things) is shared, so they are created even though they are not accidents.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why are substances (jawahir) created?
A) Because they are accidents.
B) Because they do not precede created accidents.
C) Because they are eternal.
D) Because they are composite.

Key Takeaway
Substances are created because they do not precede created accidents, sharing the cause of creation but not the cause of being accidents.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If everything that is created has a beginning, and you are created, what does that imply about your relationship to the Creator? How does this truth affect the way you live today? Will you begin to live with more awareness that you are not self-sufficient?
?
Nasafi argues that equality in one cause does not imply equality in another. Where in your life have you mistakenly assumed that because you share one trait with someone, you share all? How can this lesson correct that and lead you to a more humble assessment of yourself and others?
?
The Dahriyya denied creation. What modern ideologies or habits do you cling to that effectively deny your own createdness and dependence on God? What would it mean to fully accept that you are created and finite, and to let that reshape your priorities starting today?

The Principle of Equality in Causes
Imam Nasafi establishes the principle of equality in causes for temporality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why substances share the same temporality as accidents due to equality in the cause of temporality, and why this does not make them accidents.

Core Idea
Equality in judgments requires equality in causes, not in non-causes.

Imam Nasafi begins by affirming that substances are temporal because they share the cause of temporality with accidents. He then refutes a potential objection from the materialists by clarifying that this shared cause does not turn substances into accidents. The key distinction lies in what the cause actually is.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the main claim
The passage states that substances equal accidents in the cause of being temporal, so they are temporal. Find where this is stated.
The cause is lack of precedence.
2
Understand the example of Zayd and Amr
The author gives an analogy: if Zayd and Amr were born at the same time, and Zayd is 20 years old, then Amr must also be 20. But Zayd is not Amr. This illustrates shared temporality without shared identity.
The example clarifies the distinction.
3
Apply the principle to the objection
Notice that the materialists object that substances are not accidents. Nasafi answers by distinguishing the cause of temporality from the cause of accident status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في حد الحدوث كان مساويا إياه في الحدوث، وبهذا يبطل اعتراض الدهرية أن الجوهر لما لم يكن عرضا لأنه لم يسبق العرض لم يشاركه فيما كان لأجله عرضا فإنه بعد سبقه إياه لم يصر مستحيل البقاء ولا مفتقرا في وجوده إلى محل، فلما لم يشاركه فيما له كان العرض عرضا لم يشاركه في كونه عرضا، وهاهنا شاركه لعدم سبقه إياه فيما لأجله كان العرض حادثا، شاركه في كونه حادثا، وهذا لأن التساوي في الأحكام يكون عند التساوي في العلل لا عند التساوي في غير العلل، والجواهر لعدم السبق شاركت الأعراض في علة كونها حادثة، فكانت حادثة مثلها، ولم تشاركها في علة كونها عرضا فلم تكن عرضا، والله الموفق. مثاله: أنا لو علمنا أن ولادة زيد كانت مقترنة بولادة عمرو ثم ثبت أن زيدا ابن عشرين سنة أوجب ذلك أن يكون عمرا ابن عشرين سنة، ولم يوجب أن يكون زيد هو عمرو ولا أن ولادة زيد ولادة عمرو، فإن قيل: ثبوت حدوث الأعراض، واستحالة خلو الجوهر عنها لا يدل على حدوث الجواهر فإن كل عرض وإن كان حادثا فقبله عرض آخر هكذا إلى ما لا نهاية، هذا كما أنكم تقولون إن في الآخر تبقي الأجسام إلى ما لا نهاية، وإن كان الأجسام لا تخلو عما لا يبق من الأعراض واستحالة بقاء الأعراض واستحالة خلو الأجسام عنها لم يوجب استحالة بقاء الأجسام لا إلى نهاية لما أنه لا عرض إلا وبعده عرض لا إلى نهاية فكذا هذا في القدم، وربما يقرون هذا السؤال من وجه آخر فيقولون: لما كانت استحالة خلو الجواهر عما لا يبقى لم يوجب استحالة بقائها فاستحالة خلوها عما ليس بقديم لم يوجب استحالة قدمها. قلنا: قد بينا استحالة قدم ما لم يسبق الحوادث لمشاركته الحوادث فيما كانت لأجله حادثة والمستحيل لا يمكن تصحيحه بما يظن أنه نظيره من الممكنات بل إذا ثبت استحالة هذا بدليل مقطوع به وثبت إمكان ذلك عرف بطريق الضرورة أن بينهما مفارقة وإن جهلها الخصم، لأن الجهل عليه جائز ممكن، والخطأ على الدليل المقطوع به ممتنع، وكذا التسوية بين الممتنع والممكن ممتنعة، فكذا الحكم بجهله بالتفاوت بين الأمرين مع أن الجهل عليه أولى من الحكم ببطلان ما علم بالدليل الضروري، ثم نقول: أليس أن ما لا يتقدم على حادث واحد متعين يستحيل أن يكون قديما لمساواته إياه في المعنى الموجب للحدوث، فكذلك ما لم يسبق جميع الحوادث، وما لا يتعرى عن شيء واحد متعين يستحيل بقاؤه لا يوجب أن يستحيل بقاؤه، وكذا ما لا يتعرض عن جميع ما يستحيل بقاؤه لا يوجب استحالة بقائه، وقد ظهر لكم الفرق بين الأمرين عند الاعتبار بواحد معين من كل واحد من الجنسين، أعني ما ليس بقديم بل هو حادث وما ليس بباق ثم نقول: ما يزعمون أن لا حادث إلا وقبله حادث يوجب محالا، يوجب وجود المحدث في القدم لأن الجوهر لما كان قديما وفي قدمه لا يخلو عن الحوادث لزعم هذا أو القول بقدم المحدث ممتنع محال، لأنه قول بأن لوجوده ابتداء وليس لوجوده ابتداء، وامتناع اجتماع السلب والإيجاب في محل واحد مما لا يخفي على المجانين، فأما قولنا: إنه لا عرض إلا وبعده عرض فلا استحالة فيه، وإثبات المستحيل بثبوت ما ليس بمستحيل جهل فاحش، ولأن القول أن لا
In the definition of temporality, it was equal to it in temporality. By this, the objection of the materialists is invalidated: that since the substance was not an accident because it did not precede the accident, it did not share with it what made it an accident; for after its preceding it, it did not become impossible of permanence nor in need of a substrate for its existence. Since it did not share with it in what made the accident an accident, it did not share with it in being an accident. Here, it shared with it because it did not precede it in what made the accident temporal; it shared with it in being temporal. This is because equality in judgments occurs at equality in causes, not at equality in non-causes. Substances, for lack of precedence, shared with accidents in the cause of their being temporal, so they were temporal like them, but they did not share with them in the cause of being accidents, so they were not accidents. And God is the Guide. Example: If we knew that the birth of Zayd coincided with the birth of Amr, then it was established that Zayd is twenty years old, that would necessitate that Amr is twenty years old, but it would not necessitate that Zayd is Amr or that Zayd's birth is Amr's birth. Then it is said: The proof that accidents are temporal and the impossibility of substances being free of them does not entail substances are temporal, for every accident, though temporal, is preceded by another accident ad infinitum. This is like your saying that bodies will remain in the future endlessly, and though bodies are never free of non-permanent accidents and the impossibility of accidents' permanence and the impossibility of bodies being free of them does not necessitate the impossibility of bodies remaining endlessly, because there is no accident but is followed by an accident endlessly, so likewise this in eternity. Perhaps they present this question in another way, saying: Since the impossibility of substances being free of non-permanent accidents did not necessitate the impossibility of their permanence, so the impossibility of their being free of what is not eternal does not necessitate the impossibility of their eternity. We said: We have already shown the impossibility of the eternity of that which is not preceded by things that come to be, due to its sharing with them in what made them temporal. What is impossible cannot be rectified by what is thought to be its counterpart among possible things; rather, if the impossibility of this is established by a decisive proof, and the possibility of that is established, it is known necessarily that there is a difference between them, even if the adversary is ignorant of it. For ignorance of it is possible for him, but error regarding a decisive proof is impossible, and equating the impossible with the possible is impossible. So likewise is the judgment that his ignorance of the difference between the two matters, while ignorance of him is more appropriate than the judgment that what is known by necessary proof is false. Then we say: Is it not that what does not precede one determinate thing that comes to be is impossible to be eternal because it equals it in the meaning necessitating temporality, so likewise what does not precede all things that come to be. And what is not free of one determinate thing whose permanence is impossible does not necessitate that its permanence is impossible, and likewise what is not free of all things whose permanence is impossible does not necessitate the impossibility of its permanence. The difference between the two matters has appeared to you by consideration of one determinate from each of the two genera—I mean what is not eternal but is temporal, and what is not permanent. Then we say: What they claim—that there is no thing that comes to be but before it is a thing that comes to be—necessitates an absurdity; it necessitates the existence of the producer of things-that-come-to-be in eternity, because if the substance were eternal and in its eternity it is never free of things-that-come-to-be, according to this claim, or the statement of the eternity of what produces things-that-come-to-be is impossible and absurd, because it is a statement that its existence has a beginning and its existence does not have a beginning. The impossibility of the conjunction of negation and affirmation in one locus is not hidden even from the insane. As for our statement—that there is no accident but after it is an accident—there is no impossibility in it. And proving an impossibility by establishing what is not impossible is gross ignorance. And because the statement that no...
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit within the proof of the temporality of substances. The argument begins by restating that substances equal accidents in the cause of temporality (lack of precedence), so they are temporal. The materialists object: even if accidents are temporal and substances are never free of them, this does not prove substances are temporal, because accident sequences are infinite—each accident is preceded by another. They draw an analogy: just as bodies will remain forever despite being never free of non-permanent accidents, because accident sequences are infinite, substances could be eternal despite being never free of temporal accidents. The author then answers: we have already proven that anything not preceded by temporal things is impossible to be eternal, due to sharing the cause of temporality. The impossibility cannot be overturned by pointing to a supposed counterpart that is merely possible. If the adversary is ignorant of the difference, that is possible, but error in a decisive proof is impossible. He then distinguishes: what does not precede one determinate temporal thing cannot be eternal; similarly, what does not precede all temporal things (i.e., substances) cannot be eternal. However, what is not free of one thing that cannot remain does not imply its own permanence is impossible; but here we are talking about all temporal things. He clarifies: the claim that every temporal is preceded by another temporal leads to an absurdity: it would require the inventor of temporals to be eternal while causing temporals in eternity, which is a contradiction. Our own claim that every accident is followed by another accident is not impossible. So the objection fails.

Key Terms
حدوث
جوهر
عرض
تساوي في العلل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If substances are temporal like accidents, they must be accidents.
Correction: Temporality is caused by lack of precedence, while accident status is caused by dependence on a substrate. Sharing one cause does not imply sharing the other.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do substances not become accidents even though they share the cause of temporality?
A) Because they are not preceded by accidents.
B) Because the cause of being an accident is different from the cause of temporality.
C) Because substances are eternal.
D) Because the example of Zayd and Amr shows they are different people.

Key Takeaway
Substances are temporal because they share the cause of temporality with accidents, but they are not accidents because the cause of accidenthood is different.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you judged someone as being entirely different from you because of a superficial difference, even though you shared the same root cause (e.g., human weakness)? How does Imam Nasafi’s principle challenge you to reconsider that judgment today?
?
The materialists assumed that sharing temporality meant sharing accidenthood — they confused the cause. Is there an area in your life where you are confusing the cause of a problem with its symptoms? What step will you take to identify the true cause?
?
If equality in judgments depends on equality in causes, then what does that mean for how you compare your own deeds to others? Are you measuring by the same internal motives, or by external appearances? Ask Allah to give you insight into the true causes behind your actions.

advanced

Refuting the Objection of Infinite Accident Sequences
Imam Nasafi refutes the objection of infinite accident sequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the objection that infinite sequences of accidents allow substances to be eternal is invalid.

Core Idea
What is not preceded by all temporal things cannot be eternal.

The materialists object that even if all accidents are temporal, the fact that substances are never free of accidents does not prove substances are temporal, because accidents themselves form an infinite sequence, each preceded by another. They draw an analogy with the future endlessness of bodies. Imam Nasafi refutes this by distinguishing the impossibility of not being preceded by a single temporal from not being preceded by all, and by showing that the objection leads to absurdity.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The materialists argue: Substances are always accompanied by accidents, but accidents themselves are infinite, so substances could be eternal like bodies persist forever.
They use an analogy with body permanence.
2
Read the response
Nasafi says he has already shown that anything not preceded by all things-that-come-to-be (i.e., accidents) is temporal. The objection tries to equate that with the impossibility of bodies being free of non-permanent accidents, but that is a different case.
3
Identify the distinction
The author distinguishes between not preceding one determinate accident and not preceding all accidents. Not preceding all is impossible for an eternal being.
He also argues that the objection's claim of infinite regress leads to the absurdity of an eternal producer.
4
Reflect on the absurdity
If every accident is preceded by another, then substances in eternity would require an eternal producer causing temporal things, which is contradictory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Since accidents can be infinite, substances could be eternal if they are always with accidents.
Correction: The cause of temporality is not the presence of accidents but the lack of precedence of all temporals. Infinite regress does not remove that lack.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why does the objection of infinite accident sequences fail?
A) Because infinite sequences are impossible.
B) Because the objection confuses the cause of temporality with the cause of non-permanence.
C) Because substances are not like bodies.
D) Because the objector is ignorant.

Key Takeaway
The objection of infinite accident sequences is invalid because it misapplies the analogy and ignores the decisive proof that what does not precede all things-that-come-to-be cannot be eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted a clever objection to a truth you know simply because you couldn't see the flaw, and let that doubt linger? How does this lesson's insistence on the impossibility of error in a decisive proof challenge you to refine your own certitude?
?
If you were in a debate about God's existence and someone raised this infinite regress objection, would you be able to expose its fallacy with the precision of Imam Nasafi? What does your answer reveal about the depth of your understanding of the proof?
?
The source says 'the impossibility of the conjunction of negation and affirmation in one locus is not hidden even from the insane.' Can you think of a belief you hold that, when examined, actually contains a contradiction? Are you willing to abandon it even if it feels comfortable?
